<div id="review_1067638184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067638184" />
    <a title="Jack Tripper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper"><img alt="Jack Tripper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484547420p2/35473855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067638184?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Tripper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Tripper" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper">Jack Tripper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=desert-island-books">desert-island-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067638184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8990007982534676993">My first time reading <i>Anathem</i> was one of the most engrossing reading experiences I've ever had, in any genre. As a long-time Stepehenson fan, one could say I'm slightly biased. But, considering that I've now read this three times since it's been out, even though it's a 900+ page monstrosity, should tell you something. And I'm not one who normally rereads books.<br/><br/>First off, I should mention that it definitely helps to have even a slight interest in the 'big questions,' such as the nature of reality</span>
  <span id="freeText8990007982534676993" style="display:none">My first time reading <i>Anathem</i> was one of the most engrossing reading experiences I've ever had, in any genre. As a long-time Stepehenson fan, one could say I'm slightly biased. But, considering that I've now read this three times since it's been out, even though it's a 900+ page monstrosity, should tell you something. And I'm not one who normally rereads books.<br /><br />First off, I should mention that it definitely helps to have even a slight interest in the 'big questions,' such as the nature of reality, life, etc. If you do, this novel has some amazing concepts, interweaved throughout a great story about Erasmus, a young student/scientist living in a cloistered sanctuary for hundreds of scientists, philosophers, mathematicians, etc, on a planet called Arbre, which is similar in a lot of ways to Earth, but more advanced. These scientists are kept separate from the rest of society, with no real possessions or technology to work with, only free to leave every ten years for ten days (some sects can only leave once every 100 or 1000 years). But all that is about to change when a major threat to the planet is discovered and their help is needed in the regular world, changing their lives forever.<br /><br />Narrated in the first-person by Erasmus, <i>Anthem</i> is a breathtaking feat of worldbuilding and story. The first 100-150 pages can be a bit of a slog, as you're introduced to quite a few new words and concepts, and have to constantly go back and forth between the narrative and the glossary. After that the story grabs hold and never really lets go, at least for me. I found this to be much more of a page-tuner than Stephenson's other 21st century novels, with less bloat. The discursions are somewhat held in check here, and always related to the story in some way, even if it doesn't seem so at times.<br /><br />As I mentioned, there are a lot of philosophical concepts discussed, but much of it is between two or more characters, called 'dialogs,' in which the conversation is almost like a battle, with one gaining the upper hand, the other losing. This makes these sections fun, almost like action scenes, rather than a chore. There's plenty of real action as well, and an adventure that spans the globe, and beyond (it's hard, but I'm REALLY trying not to give anything away), with some of the best characters of Stephenson's career. Oh, and it actually has an entirely satisfying ending, which is quite refreshing, and somewhat unique as far as Stephenson is concerned.<br /><br />Anyone looking for an epic sf adventure with some great characters and far-out concepts, not to mention a world that's fully realized and richly detailed, owes it to themselves to read this. It's a novel that demands constant attention while reading, but it's one I will never forget, and I'll most likely read it again and again in the future. It transports me to another world in a way that few have ever done, to the point where at times I'd forget I'm reading, I'm so immersed in the world of Arbre. I don't know if there's higher praise than that for fans of great worldbuilding in sci-fi or fantasy.<br /><br />5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="8990007982534676993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21928755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21928755" />
    <a title="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for"><img alt="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442455304p2/834216.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21928755?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" class="user" itemprop="url" name="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" href="/user/show/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for">This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061474101" href="/book/show/6250159-anathem">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=locus-award">locus-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21928755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8170150368845251113"><i>Anathem</i> is another incredible book by Neal Stephenson, although probably not for everyone. Highly philosophical, brimming with hard science, it is the story of a world where scientists have been more-or-less sequestered for centuries in "maths" (the scientific equivalent of a monastery), living ascetic lives and devising high philosophy of the universe. It is the story of a specific Avout (=monk), Erasmus, and what happens when the world that they know is turned upside down by an unexpected thre</span>
  <span id="freeText8170150368845251113" style="display:none"><i>Anathem</i> is another incredible book by Neal Stephenson, although probably not for everyone. Highly philosophical, brimming with hard science, it is the story of a world where scientists have been more-or-less sequestered for centuries in "maths" (the scientific equivalent of a monastery), living ascetic lives and devising high philosophy of the universe. It is the story of a specific Avout (=monk), Erasmus, and what happens when the world that they know is turned upside down by an unexpected threat (I'm being deliberately vague to avoid spoilers).<br /><br />For many people, the plot may drag (it is a long book with almost 900 pages of text), particularly given that so much of the book is filled with philosophical discourse and discussion (almost always important to the story, although often is its not obvious how or why until much later). Stephenson also invented many words to express slightly unique concepts or to frame well known concepts in slightly different language. For example, "the reticulum" is used for the book's equivalent of the internet. The title, "Anathem" is a deliberate mix of the words "Anthem" and "Anathema". This can make the reading, particularly at the beginning (say maybe the first 100 pages or so) as one is settling into the story and the plot is largely put aside for background and setting, a bit more complicated and potentially frustrating for some readers (although there is a very useful Glossary of many of these words at the back of the book). <br /><br /><i>Anathem</i> suffers some of the same pretentions as The Baroque Cycle (<i>Quicksilver, The Confusion,</i> and <i>System of the World</i>), but not nearly to such an extreme and will likely be much more enjoyable to most readers. Personally, I probably put this as his second best book, with #1 being <i>Cryptonomicon</i>, which I think is generally tighter and more approachable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8170150368845251113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2447083171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447083171" />
    <a title="Eye of Sauron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61597976-eye-of-sauron"><img alt="Eye of Sauron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479408483p2/61597976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447083171?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eye of Sauron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eye of Sauron" href="/user/show/61597976-eye-of-sauron">Eye of Sauron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Eye of Sauron by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=five-star-novels">five-star-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=top-25-novels">top-25-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=top-100-novels">top-100-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61597976-eye-of-sauron?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447083171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17167848328937584766">WOW.<br/><br/>Farewell, YA Fantasy; I don't believe I'm ever coming back.<br/><br/><b>This is one fantastic book.</b> Stephenson combines philosophy, mystery, science fiction, fantasy, anthropology, satire, and a lot more in what is probably one of my new favorite books of all time. Certainly the best novel I've read that was written post-2000. <br/><br/><i>Anathem</i>'s worldbuilding (physical, cultural, historical, philosophical, etc.) is brilliant. The <i>concent of the avout</i> idea is pretty much my idea of a utopia: it's a massive, comple</span>
  <span id="freeText17167848328937584766" style="display:none">WOW.<br /><br />Farewell, YA Fantasy; I don't believe I'm ever coming back.<br /><br /><b>This is one fantastic book.</b> Stephenson combines philosophy, mystery, science fiction, fantasy, anthropology, satire, and a lot more in what is probably one of my new favorite books of all time. Certainly the best novel I've read that was written post-2000. <br /><br /><i>Anathem</i>'s worldbuilding (physical, cultural, historical, philosophical, etc.) is brilliant. The <i>concent of the avout</i> idea is pretty much my idea of a utopia: it's a massive, complex societal structure whose members' primary function is <b>philosophizing</b>. They have no currency and few personal possessions, and basically embody what would happen if Plato's Academy grew to eat the world. They regularly and casually engage in Dialog, which is a logical and rhetorical debate in which the participants take nothing for granted and attempt to find truth while "planing" each other. I LOVE IT.<br /><br />Stephenson clearly took many of his ideas from Western philosophical tradition, with lots of little nods to Plato, Aristotle, Einstein, Jules Verne, and many others. The avout even have their own slightly different version of Occam's Razor, which they call the Steelyard. Much of the book consists of these formal Dialogs, but they are <b>absolutely fascinating</b>. What is consciousness? Why do we worry? How valid is the multiverse theory? Does time exist? Do we exist? (All of these are important to the plot, by the way, not just random rabbit trails.)<br /><br />I'm not doing this justice. If it sounds at all interesting to you, you should absolutely read it. Although it is 900+ pages long, it's worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17167848328937584766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V9b2DV7xTpjCygazRQLYQIemdnnkls72HKAHVmucughJWQDNvq/ltNGLXSqi8sLSC9jh4qX1pFE5LHcQFwraog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('76rpnZyxFgxd30ppZJpLcagx3S8TfqhKPw1s/RTdrHDxJR9dfO+9IE6eEfCDalHjJE9KtFIdwu0agRy7aEvM2g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14445805912265955566">Neal Stephenson is the author of <i>Reamde, Anathem,</i> and the three-volume historical epic the Baroque Cycle (<i>Quicksilver, The Confusion,</i> and <i>The System of the World</i>), as well as <i>Cryptonomicon, The Diamond Age, Snow Crash,</i> and <i>Zodiac.</i> He lives in Seattle, Washington.</span>
